## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of concentration A, so the task is to infer a kinetic rate law of the form dA_dt = f(t, A). With only t and A available, common structures include order-based power laws in A and time-dependent effective rate constants capturing deactivation, forcing, or non-ideal kinetics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption when reactant is in excess or surface/catalyst-limited)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, pseudo-first-order kinetics)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with equal/reactant-limited conditions reduced to a single concentration)
- nth-order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/generalized reaction order)
- Autocatalytic/self-accelerating kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (growth-like accumulation of A via autocatalysis or formation pathways)
- Relaxation to equilibrium (linear driving force): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state or equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalysis with self-limitation: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-form kinetics; growth at low A, saturation near c1)
- Saturating consumption (Michaelis-type without explicit substrate variable): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate limited by a finite-capacity step such as adsorption/catalyst sites)
- Inhibition/retardation rational form: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (self-inhibition or crowding/viscosity effects increasing with A)
- Time-dependent pseudo-first-order constant (exponential deactivation): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation or activity loss over time)
- Time-dependent pseudo-first-order constant (power-law aging): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (anomalous/fractal kinetics where effective rate varies as a power of time)
- Time-dependent pseudo-first-order constant (hyperbolic slowdown): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * t) (gradual slowing due to deactivation, fouling, or transport limitation increasing with time)
- Externally driven kinetics (periodic forcing): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (photochemical modulation, mixing cycles, pulsed input affecting the effective rate)
- Polynomial-in-time effective rate: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t + c2 * t**2) * A (empirical time-programmed conditions causing nonstationary first-order behavior)
- Log-time slowing: dA_dt = -c0 * log(c1 + c2 * t) * A (rates that increase/decrease slowly with time due to cumulative changes in medium or morphology)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over a range of A, a zero-order term (-c0) is likely (rate controlled by something other than A).
- If dA_dt scales proportionally with A (straight line in dA_dt vs A), a first-order structure (-c0*A) is suggested; curvature indicates higher/lower effective order.
- If the magnitude of dA_dt grows faster than linearly with A, include A**c1 with c1 > 1 (higher-order/chain or bimolecular-like behavior).
- If dA_dt changes sign and crosses zero at A ≈ constant, use a driving-force-to-equilibrium term (A - c1), indicating a stable steady state at A = c1.
- If growth/decay slows as A becomes large and approaches an upper bound, include a self-limiting factor like (c1 - A) or a rational saturation A/(A+c1).
- If increasing A reduces the effective rate (self-inhibition), rational forms like A/(1 + c1*A) capture rate suppression at high A.
- If apparent kinetics drift over time even at similar A, include an explicit time-dependent prefactor (e.g., exp(-c*t), 1/(1+c*t), or t**c) to represent deactivation/aging/conditioning.
- If there are oscillations or periodic features in dA_dt vs t, include sinusoidal forcing multiplying a baseline rate (1 + c*sin(c*t)).
- If the rate changes slowly with time (sublinear trends), log(c1 + c2*t) or weak power-law-in-time modifiers can represent gradual medium evolution or transport-regime shifts.

Best expression     : A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t)
Structure desc      : Two-term additive model: cube-root in A plus A times a decaying exponential in t. A participates as A^{1/3} (slow growth) and linearly multiplied by exp(-0.0783 t); t appears only in the exponential factor. With c1=-0.675 dominating typical magnitudes, the main behavior is an A-proportional term whose strength decays with t, plus a smaller positive 0.208·A^{1/3}. Approximate form is exactly 0.208 A^{1/3} - 0.675 A e^{-0.0783 t} (no degeneracy).
Fitted params       : c0=2.0847e-01, c1=-6.7505e-01, c2=-7.8313e-02

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK17)

GT: -c0*A*exp(-c1*_s*t) + c2*_f*A**c3
Candidate formulas: 60

GT is the fixed function
\[
F(t,A)=0.2084703204063362\,A^{1/3}\;-\;0.6750544468008356\,A\,e^{-0.0783132263146032\,t}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly** “(constant)\(\cdot A^{1/3}\) + (constant)\(\cdot A\exp(\text{constant}\cdot t)\)” with **no extra nonzero terms**, and with the exponential rate negative.

---

### 1. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t)`
Matches form exactly. Choose  
- \(c0=0.2084703204063362\)  
- \(c1=-0.6750544468008356\)  
- \(c2=-0.0783132263146032\).  
✅ Equivalent.

### 2. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1*sqrt(A**2)*exp(c2*t)`
\(\sqrt{A^2}=|A|\), not \(A\). GT has \(A\), not \(|A|\). No constant choice makes \(|A| \equiv A\) for all real \(A\).  
❌ Not equivalent.

### 3. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*log(A*c4 + 1)`
Extra \(\log(\cdot)\) term must vanish for all \(A\). Set \(c3=0\). Then reduces to candidate 1, which can match.  
✅ Equivalent (with \(c3=0\) and same \(c0,c1,c2\) as #1).

### 4. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3/(c4*t + c5) + c6/(c4*t + c5)`
Rational-in-\(t\) terms must vanish for all \(t\). Set \(c3=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then reduces to candidate 1.  
✅ Equivalent.

### 5. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*exp(A*c4)`
Extra \(e^{A c4}\) must vanish: set \(c3=0\). Then reduces to candidate 1.  
✅ Equivalent.

### 6. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3`
Extra constant must be 0: set \(c3=0\). Then reduces to candidate 1.  
✅ Equivalent.

### 7. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1 + c2*sqrt(A**2)*exp(c3*t)`
Has \(|A|e^{c3 t}\) plus an additive constant \(c1\). To match GT we’d need \(|A|=A\) for all \(A\) (impossible) and also \(c1=0\).  
❌ Not equivalent.

### 8. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A**c3*c4`
Extra power term must vanish: set \(c4=0\). Then reduces to candidate 1.  
✅ Equivalent.

### 9. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*t**c4 + c5`
Extra \(t\)-power and constant must vanish: set \(c3=0\) and \(c5=0\). Then reduces to candidate 1.  
✅ Equivalent.

### 10. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1 + c2*t**c3 + c4*sqrt(A**2)*exp(c5*t)`
Again uses \(|A|\) not \(A\); also extra \(c1\) and \(t^{c3}\) term. Even if those are zeroed, \(|A|\neq A\) globally.  
❌ Not equivalent.

### 11. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + c3*log(A*c4 + 1) + c5`
Set \(c3=0, c5=0\) → candidate 1.  
✅ Equivalent.

### 12. `A**(1/3)*c0 + c1 + c2*sqrt(A**2)*exp(c3*t) + c4*log(A*c5 + 1)`
Contains \(|A|\) term; cannot become \(A\) for all \(A\).  
❌ Not equivalent.

### 13. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*(c2 + t)**c3 + c4 + c5*sqrt(A**2)*exp(c6*t)`
Has \((t+c2)^{c3}\) instead of \(e^{kt}\), and also \(|A|e^{c6 t}\). Can’t transform power into exponential for all \(t\) via constants.  
❌ Not equivalent.

### 14. `A**(1/3)*c0 + A*c1*exp(c2*t) + A*c3*(c4 + t)**c5 + c6`

**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**
